  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3c22bbc5-d63c-45bd-be9b-0d1cdf09029e'
      });

  <span id="freeText3427360503472065102" style="display:none">Jeanne, ayant fini ses malles, s'approcha de la fenêtre, mais la pluie ne cessait pas.<br />L'averse, toute la nuit, avait sonné contre les carreaux et les toits. Le ronflement des ruisseaux débordés emplissait les rues désertes où les maisons, comme des éponges, buvaient l'humidité qui pénétrait au-dedans et faisait suer les murs de la cave au grenier.</span>

<div id="review_1490279626" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1490279626" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1490279626?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/1452645.Une_vie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=1001-books-to-read-before-you-die">1001-books-to-read-before-you-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1490279626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15557425307325125226">One of those absolutely beautiful books that leave me almost at a loss for words.<br/><br/>So well-written, in beautifully flowing French, and such a hard topic: a woman's lack of choice in 19th century conventional society. A <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2175.Madame_Bovary' title='Madame Bovary by Gustave Flaubert' rel='nofollow noopener'>Madame Bovary</a> without the energetic, yet fatalistic drive to change her condition, Maupassant's Jeanne suffers as much, but has a lot less adventure and passion to remember at the end of her life. She is proof that you indeed regret what you didn't do. Even the suffering 19th centur</span>
  <span id="freeText15557425307325125226" style="display:none">One of those absolutely beautiful books that leave me almost at a loss for words.<br /><br />So well-written, in beautifully flowing French, and such a hard topic: a woman's lack of choice in 19th century conventional society. A <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2175.Madame_Bovary" title="Madame Bovary by Gustave Flaubert" rel="nofollow noopener">Madame Bovary</a> without the energetic, yet fatalistic drive to change her condition, Maupassant's Jeanne suffers as much, but has a lot less adventure and passion to remember at the end of her life. She is proof that you indeed regret what you didn't do. Even the suffering 19th century girl breaking down over the symbolic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/775616.The_Yellow_Wallpaper" title="The Yellow Wallpaper by Charlotte Perkins Gilman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Yellow Wallpaper</a> has more choice than Jeanne, who remains entirely passive in her dominant social environment.<br /><br />The tragic feeling of loneliness never leaves the main character, and alienation from the rest of the world is the theme of her life:<br /><br />"Elle sentait entre elle et lui comme un voile, un obstacle, s’apercevant pour la première fois que deux personnes ne se pénètrent jamais jusqu’à l’âme, jusqu’au fond des pensées, qu’elles marchent côté à côté, enlacées parfois, mais non mêlées, et que l’être moral de chacun de nous reste éternellement seul pour la vie."<br /><br />Sad, beautiful, must-read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15557425307325125226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1170425550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16401182747543327780"><br/>Compared to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/780581.Bel_Ami' title='Bel-Ami by Guy de Maupassant' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bel-Ami</a>, this was a slower-paced read, but the writing is nonetheless beautiful. I was captivated by Maupassant's sensitivities in his descriptive skills in general. <br/><br/>It is a carefully crafted story of an aristocratic lady with a sheltered bring-up who has lived through shattered dreams about love, unhappiness in marriage, betrayals by husband, best friend and friends, disillusions with the mores of her times and disappointment with life in general. Maupassant writes with compassion w</span>
  <span id="freeText16401182747543327780" style="display:none"><br />Compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/780581.Bel_Ami" title="Bel-Ami by Guy de Maupassant" rel="nofollow noopener">Bel-Ami</a>, this was a slower-paced read, but the writing is nonetheless beautiful. I was captivated by Maupassant's sensitivities in his descriptive skills in general. <br /><br />It is a carefully crafted story of an aristocratic lady with a sheltered bring-up who has lived through shattered dreams about love, unhappiness in marriage, betrayals by husband, best friend and friends, disillusions with the mores of her times and disappointment with life in general. Maupassant writes with compassion where the protagonist is concerned, and with clear-sighted satire on the subject of religion and dogmas.<br /><br />The setting is mainly in a seaside suburb of Rouen with some diversion to the island of Corsica, all beautifully portrayed. The times are in the early 19th century.<br /><br />I was totally transported by the writing, whether it was the twists and turns of the story, or the enthralling descriptions of thoughts and emotions, or the refined painting of places and scenes. My only complaint is that the ending seemed to be a bit abrupt.<br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>

<div id="review_63179227" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63179227" />
    <a title="El" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83144-el"><img alt="El" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479156984p2/83144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63179227?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El" href="/user/show/83144-el">El</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780192832986" href="/book/show/128618.A_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=19th-centurylit-late">19th-centurylit-late</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=1001-books-list">1001-books-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63179227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4373947456989095145">Jeanne grew up in a sheltered life, being the heiress to a fortune and having gone to school at a convent. After finishing school she meets Viscount de Lamare who woos her, weds her and takes her off to Corsica for a spectacular honeymoon. Upon returning from France Jeanne finds her new husband is not quite the man she expected. Her naivety is overwhelming at times, but clearly that is point. We follow Jeanne's life through all of her disillusionment across the years into her senior years. She n</span>
  <span id="freeText4373947456989095145" style="display:none">Jeanne grew up in a sheltered life, being the heiress to a fortune and having gone to school at a convent. After finishing school she meets Viscount de Lamare who woos her, weds her and takes her off to Corsica for a spectacular honeymoon. Upon returning from France Jeanne finds her new husband is not quite the man she expected. Her naivety is overwhelming at times, but clearly that is point. We follow Jeanne's life through all of her disillusionment across the years into her senior years. She never quite shakes the rose-tinted glasses off her eyes and the reader feels simultaneously sorry for and angry at her for it.<br /><br />Being the first novel written by Maupassant it's a rather decent book, though as an early novel it's clear to see why he's better known for his short stories. The attempt at character development falls short since Jeanne remains relatively the same throughout the story. Maupassant's descriptions of landscapes are probably the best part of the book, and surprisingly he delves into a blatant sexual territory (complete with orgasms outdoors!).<br /><br />As a parody of contemporaries of Maupassant and the novels written before 1883 this is really a fun book. The important thing is not to take it too seriously because you <i>will</i> want to smack the shit out of Jeanne.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4373947456989095145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2979184582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2979184582" />
    <a title="TBV" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/98589549-tbv"><img alt="TBV" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560644618p2/98589549.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2979184582?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TBV" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TBV" href="/user/show/98589549-tbv">TBV</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42711681-une-vie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/98589549-tbv?shelf=in-french">in-french</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/98589549-tbv?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/98589549-tbv?shelf=reviewed-2019">reviewed-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/98589549-tbv?shelf=favourites-2019">favourites-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/98589549-tbv?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2979184582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6531473629041422096">Upon completion of her convent education at the age of seventeen, Jeanne is taken home by her father to start her adult life. Jeanne, wearing metaphorical rose tinted spectacles, is dreaming of a future of romance, a happy marriage and two children - a boy followed not long after by a girl. Jeanne's wealthy parents are providing her with a property of her own. So it seems that she is off to a good start.<br/><br/>But is she? Things don't go entirely to plan, and she soon learns about love and life. It is </span>
  <span id="freeText6531473629041422096" style="display:none">Upon completion of her convent education at the age of seventeen, Jeanne is taken home by her father to start her adult life. Jeanne, wearing metaphorical rose tinted spectacles, is dreaming of a future of romance, a happy marriage and two children - a boy followed not long after by a girl. Jeanne's wealthy parents are providing her with a property of her own. So it seems that she is off to a good start.<br /><br />But is she? Things don't go entirely to plan, and she soon learns about love and life. It is not so very long before her fresh joyful attitude changes to cynicism: <i>"Tout n’était donc que misère, chagrin, malheur et mort. Tout trompait, tout mentait, tout faisait souffrir et pleurer."</i><br /><br />And every time you think that things can't get worse they do...<br /><br />Clouds are said to have silver linings, and fortunately Jeanne has them in the form of supportive parents and the maid Rosalie. It is ultimately Rosalie who tells Jeanne that <i> "La vie, voyez-vous, ça n’est jamais si bon ni si mauvais qu’on croit."</i><br /><br />De Maupassant is known as a master of short story writing, but he certainly knew how to write longer works too. I can't vouch for any translation, but in the original French the writing is just beautiful! Maupassant deftly uses nature and the elements to provide not only a marvellous atmosphere and beautiful descriptions, but also for example to create a sense of foreboding in his description of autumn. He creates a story of the ordinary life of an ordinary girl, but oh, what a dismal life!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6531473629041422096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780192832986" href="/book/show/128618.A_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542098385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3662422699607881729">I love Maupassant and always find he tackles the timeless difficult issues of life, that resonate down through the ages, with masterly and devastating acuity. The ‘life’ we examine is that of Jeanne, a naive young country girl, born into a life of privilege and convent educated, but destined to misfortune and tragedy. Poor Jeanne who is slow to acquire any degree of self knowledge and never really understands the realities of the life with all its brutal contradictions, and so is a ‘victim’ in d</span>
  <span id="freeText3662422699607881729" style="display:none">I love Maupassant and always find he tackles the timeless difficult issues of life, that resonate down through the ages, with masterly and devastating acuity. The ‘life’ we examine is that of Jeanne, a naive young country girl, born into a life of privilege and convent educated, but destined to misfortune and tragedy. Poor Jeanne who is slow to acquire any degree of self knowledge and never really understands the realities of the life with all its brutal contradictions, and so is a ‘victim’ in devastating fashion. <br /><br />Her early life is idyllic and she lives with adoring parents in beautiful seclusion in a chateau in Normandy on an estate by the sea, “..facing her was a broad lawn as yellow as butter under the night sky. Two tall trees rose up like steeples in front of the house, a plane to the north and a linden to the south….. Jeanne gazed at the broad surface of the sea, which looked like watered silk, sleeping peacefully under the stars. In the quiet of the sunless sky all the scents of the earth rose up into the air. A jessamine climbing round the downstairs windows gave a penetrating scent, which mingled with the fainter smell of the young leaves. Gentle gusts of wind were blowing, laden with the sharp tang of the salt and the heavy sticky reek of seaweed. At first the girl was happy just breathing the night air; the peace of the countryside had the calming effect of a cool bath.”<br /><br />From daydreaming and being a free spirited youth where ‘her whole childhood at the convent had been taken up with the future, and she had busied herself with fantasies’ but reality stalks her upon her wedding night, and all her illusions are shattered when her Father suddenly draws off our spirited young innocent to invoke her submission, “.. remember this and only this, you belong totally to your husband” , and from that point onward poor Jeanne is wracked by the vicissitudes of a cruel world she doesn’t understand and knows, only fleetingly, love and happiness, but experiences at great length loss, betrayal and humiliation. <br /><br />From this moment onward the life of the poor ingénue disintegrates and degradation follows, and after a short lived romance, surrounded by greed and avarice, she is given over to despair, “She believed herself to be so directly the target of unrelenting misfortune that she became as fatalistic as an Oriental; and the habitual experience of seeing all her hopes and dreams crumble and vanish meant that she shrank from all further endeavour.”<br /><br />The author shows the slow disintegration that follows and the complete demoralisation of the young girl now become the embittered middle aged woman, “Sometimes she would spend the whole afternoon sitting looking at the sea; sometimes she went down to Yport through the wood, repeating the walks of old days which she could not forget. What a long time it was since she had wondered through the countryside as a young girl intoxicated with dreams!”<br /><br />Those closest to her will disappoint and betray her and she is shocked and repelled, "at the cravenness of human beings, slaves to the foul procedures of carnal love that makes cowards of the heart as well as the body. Mankind seemed to her unclean when she thought of all the dirty secrets of the senses, the degrading caresses, and the dimly discerned mysteries of inseparable couplings.”<br /><br />Not just a coming of age novel but a slow crumbling of the edifices of love and marriage, organised religion and human greed; Maupassant lays bare the ugly side of life with all its degradation and disappointment, in chilling and controversial (too explicit for its time) fashion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3662422699607881729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13424936293400262166">It had good lessons, but it was not an enjoyable or good read at all. My dad gave a nice copy of this book to me for Christmas. Five months later, I finally got around to reading it. It was a terrible, depressing book. Even after I reported most of the horrendous plot, my dad only said, "It's good for her." I would not recommend this book to girls my age. The main character, Jeanne, is surrounded by evil, wanton people. She seems to be the only good person in the whole book, but of course she wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13424936293400262166" style="display:none">It had good lessons, but it was not an enjoyable or good read at all. My dad gave a nice copy of this book to me for Christmas. Five months later, I finally got around to reading it. It was a terrible, depressing book. Even after I reported most of the horrendous plot, my dad only said, "It's good for her." I would not recommend this book to girls my age. The main character, Jeanne, is surrounded by evil, wanton people. She seems to be the only good person in the whole book, but of course she was naive and thoughtless and weak. In the book a woman said something to her that I thought summed up the cause of most of her ruined life: "You've made a bad marriage, that's the whole secret. One has no business to marry without knowing anything about one's husband." It was hard to watch a blooming young woman change into a ruined, penniless, abandoned old woman. But it's by Maupassant. What did I expect? <br /></span>

<div id="review_2105192667" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2105192667" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48327873-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449341848p2/48327873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2105192667?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/48327873-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9782253004240" href="/book/show/18656770-une-vie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48327873-markus?shelf=classic-fictions">classic-fictions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48327873-markus?shelf=read-in-french">read-in-french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2105192667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17889520672512687961">Une Vie<br/>Maupassant (1850 – 1893)<br/>If you were expecting to read the happy story of the life of a beautiful young lady from the age of sixteen to forty-six, you will be seriously disappointed. <br/>Maupassant has worked out in detail everything that could go wrong and will go wrong. <br/> A life of grief, misfortune, and destruction of everything a young person innocently hopes for when leaving the convent where she had her noble and religious education. <br/>Jeanne, cherished and the only daughter of Baron Le Per</span>
  <span id="freeText17889520672512687961" style="display:none">Une Vie<br />Maupassant (1850 – 1893)<br />If you were expecting to read the happy story of the life of a beautiful young lady from the age of sixteen to forty-six, you will be seriously disappointed. <br />Maupassant has worked out in detail everything that could go wrong and will go wrong. <br /> A life of grief, misfortune, and destruction of everything a young person innocently hopes for when leaving the convent where she had her noble and religious education. <br />Jeanne, cherished and the only daughter of Baron Le Perthuis des Vauds, had every reason to hope for a bright and happy life. And so it seemed at first. Just four month after her return the family castle on a clifftop in Normandy, she is presented and swiftly married to a new neighbor, the young and good looking Viscount de Lamare. <br />Honeymoon on the isle of Corsica was her first and last encounter with love and happiness.<br />As soon as the young couple had returned to the family property ‘The Poplars’, the life of Jeanne was behind her. <br />Her husband changed personality overnight, rejected Jeanne, preferred to have his own bedroom, spent his time hunting and became physically neglected, dirty, bearded, unkempt and rude in every way.<br />The baron and his wife had gone to live in another property in Rouen. <br />One day, to Jeanne’s great surprise, on the floor of her bedroom, Rosalie her maid since childhood, gives birth to a child, a boy, she cries without end and refuses to tell the name of its father. <br />Jeanne’s husband getting into a rage of fury, wants the maid to be chased away with her bundle, without further delay.<br />Jeanne calls her parents for help, who in turn call the parish priest for advice and Rosalie is further pressed and reveals the child’s father, who is no other than Julien, Jeanne’s husband.<br />Jeanne is devastated and her family now turns against Julien, but the priest knows how to smooth those waves, in hinting at some secret knowledge he has, from sins of the older generation. <br />Rosalie is also forgiven and with the gift of a small farmstead, a young husband is found, willing to marry Rosalie with a child. <br />Jeanne at this time realizes that she too is expecting and soon gives birth to the legitimate child, a boy, to be named Paul. She turns all her attention and love to the child. <br />When Jeanne’s old mother dies, her sorrow is without limit until she discovers in her mother’s old papers, some secret love letters establishing the truth, her mother also had a secret lover in her youth. Jeanne is heartbroken and destroys all these letters, to avoid her father to get to know them also.<br />Meanwhile, Julien, the Viscount has discovered another lady to pursue, wife of some noble neighbor. Following the priest's advice, Jeanne passes the information secretly to the deceived husband, who in a rage of jealousy assassinates the adulterous couple. <br />Jeanne now has to live with the knowledge that, even though through another meddling of the priest, she was the key to that act of fury. <br />Fifteen years go by, and young Paul is growing up. After some years of college, where he spends little attention, he runs away with a young woman to London first and then to Paris.<br />He spends money without counting, asking his mother for help every time he is in need.<br />At first by the thousands, then by ten thousand and in the end several hundred thousand francs. He now threatens to commit suicide if he cannot be helped.<br />Jeanne calls her old father for help. In the end, all their fortune is lost and spent, even the castle had to be sold. The old baron dies of grief, and Jeanne falls ill and almost loses her mind. <br />Rosalie, her maid, turns up at the baron’s funeral and now takes care of Jeanne.<br />At this point, the downward spiral of the story finally stops. <br />Rosalie, now over forty, same age as Jeanne, has grown to a strong woman and her good common sense knows how to handle Paul and his money problems. <br />In the end, the very good news is the arrival of a little girl, Paul's daughter, and Jeanne's granddaughter. <br />It was about time to read something good in this story. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17889520672512687961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_96560997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96560997" />
    <a title="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof"><img alt="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268256340p2/1253478.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96560997?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" href="/user/show/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof">The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140441611" href="/book/show/1032112.A_Woman_s_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96560997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5136082079586910222">Who would have thought that such a little book (just 202 pages) could incite so many different emotions (on the part of the reader as well as the characters). One minutes I was swooning over landscape and seascape and melting in Maupassants prose, and the next I was wanting to ring the protagonists neck!<br/><br/>The book starts with a young Jeanne who is on her last ever day at the convent school in 1819 and who is desperate to taste freedom and start her life after being cooped up for so long, only bein</span>
  <span id="freeText5136082079586910222" style="display:none">Who would have thought that such a little book (just 202 pages) could incite so many different emotions (on the part of the reader as well as the characters). One minutes I was swooning over landscape and seascape and melting in Maupassants prose, and the next I was wanting to ring the protagonists neck!<br /><br />The book starts with a young Jeanne who is on her last ever day at the convent school in 1819 and who is desperate to taste freedom and start her life after being cooped up for so long, only being able to stare out of windows and dream what her life will be like when she is finally out in the world. Jeanne’s daydreams are filled with longing and a restless spirit that is aching to see far away lands and nature and finally breathe after all these years at school. Jeanne’s parents (a Baron and Baroness) pick her up on her last day and drive her to Poplars which is to become her home by the sea. Maupassants narrative is so beautiful in parts that I longed to be there too; to experience what Jeanne was experiencing.<br /><br /><i> “First of all facing her was a broad lawn as yellow as butter under the night sky. Two tall trees rose up like steeples in front of the hous, a plane to the north and a linden to the south.”<br /><br />“Jeanne gazed at the broad surface of the sea, which looked like watered silk, sleeping peacefully under the stars. In the quiet of the sunless sky all the scents of the earth rose up into the air. A jessamine climbing round the downstairs windows gave a penetrating scent, which mingled with the fainter smell of the young leaves. Gentle gusts of wind were blowing, laden with the sharp tang of the salt and the heavy sticky reek of seaweed. At first the girl was happy just breathing the night air; the peace of the countryside had the calming effect of a cool bath.” </i><br /><br />Jeanne’s first few months are spent getting to know her new surroundings and enjoying her freedom and soon she is introduced to a young man by the name of Julien who is a count and after a breif and all-consuming romance they marry. Jeanne starts to pick up clues that all is not what it seemed as early as the wedding night when he forces himself on his new bride but desperately wanting to believe that she has married the right man and stay happy she puts it to one side. I feel the need to note here (for amusements sake) that Julien calls his wifes breasts <b> Mr Sleeper-out </b> and <b> Mr Kiss-me-quick </b>and certain other part of her womanly anatomy <b> The road to Damascus.</b> Fortunatley these aren’t mentioned more than once.<br /><br />The story is very much about the downward spiral of one woman’s life. We watch Jeanne’s hopes and desires and dreams turn into boredom and frustration and self-pity.<br /><br /><i> “Suddenly she realised that she had nothing to do and never would have anything.”<br /><br />“But now the magic reality of those first days was about to become the every day reality, which closed the door on those hopes and delightful enigmas of the unknown.”<br /><br />“Habit spread over her life like a layer of resignation like the chalky deposit left on the ground by certain kinds of of water.”<br /><br />“Sometimes she would spend the whole afternoon sitting looking at the sea; sometimes she went down to Yport through the wood, repeating the walks of old days which she could not forget. What a long time it was since she had wondered through the countryside as a young girl intoxicated with dreams!” </i><br /><br />Maupassant has such a way with words that he drew me into Jeanne’s world and I felt the same longing she felt. It took me back to days when I had the world at my feet too and thought I could do anything, had no cares in the world – OK so my carefree days were a little different to Jeanne’s as in rather than floating round some big mansion by the sea, it was made up of nights out on the town, no mortgage to pay and a feeling of being able accountable to nobody except myself (ahh, to be so naive once more!). I do sometimes wonder how I would have coped in those days – one part of me thinks how lovely to do nothing all day other than read my books and take little walks round the garden with my parasol in hand, and the other part thinks but what would happen when you got bored of that? A woman didn’t have a choice then. In those particular circles they were there to look pretty and be seen but not so much heard. How dull!<br /><br />Despite my sympathy towards Jeanne, not just because of her longing for something else but also because of her brutish husband and selfish son, I still found myself wanting to grab her shoulders and give her a good shake! My God, this woman can make a fuss. Her level of self-pity knows no bounds – we have hysterics, weeping, falling on someones breast and weeping, collapsing on a chair and weeping, we have fainting, panic attacks and wailing. There were times when I wanted to yell “get a grip, love!” at the pages. <br /><br /><i> “She continually repeated: ‘I have no luck in life.’ But Rosalie would retort: ‘What would you say if you had to earn your living and had to get up at six every morning and go out to work? There are plenty of women who have to do that, and when they are too old to work, they starve to death.’” </i><br /><br />Quite!<br /><br />This book, I believe, should have been translated as One Woman’s Life rather than A Woman’s Life as it is very much about Jeanne and her personal story. <br /><br />I read quite a few Maupassant books when I was at school (we studied Boule de Suife and some of his other shorter stories) but it’s far too long since I have read anything else of his. I’m glad I did – it reminded me why I liked him. Recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5136082079586910222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_393723209" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393723209" />
    <a title="Randy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10072352-randy"><img alt="Randy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369269423p2/10072352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393723209?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Randy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Randy" href="/user/show/10072352-randy">Randy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393723209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16436283808750787989">This is realism. Reality can be harsh, especially to the unprepared. Our "heroine" Jeanne has spent much of her young life in a convent school, which has shielded her from the coming realities of life as wife, mother, family survivor. Sometimes translators/editors would similarly shield us from the complete contents of a work.<br/><br/>I originally had the misfortune of buying a "complete works" set of Maupassant to discover entire significant passages had been cut out, bowdlerized, to protect us from the</span>
  <span id="freeText16436283808750787989" style="display:none">This is realism. Reality can be harsh, especially to the unprepared. Our "heroine" Jeanne has spent much of her young life in a convent school, which has shielded her from the coming realities of life as wife, mother, family survivor. Sometimes translators/editors would similarly shield us from the complete contents of a work.<br /><br />I originally had the misfortune of buying a "complete works" set of Maupassant to discover entire significant passages had been cut out, bowdlerized, to protect us from the information the author was trying to finally bring to light. I was alerted to this by a reviewer, and I began to compare different editions of works I'd obtained. Which is not to say that this edition is the only edition that is complete, but caveat emptor. Many readers have been bored, "put off," disillusioned by a poorly translated or heavily edited edition.<br /><br />A good case in point is made by one omission in a particular translation of A Woman's Life. A "good marriage" has been agreed upon by Jeanne, her parents, and a local scion. The marriage is "good" because it joins two land-owning families together--with the added benefit of the couple seemingly enchanted by one another. The night of the wedding, Jeanne's father takes her for a stroll:<br /><br />"Darling, I have a difficult part to play, which is really your mother's; but, as she refuses, it devolves on me. I do not know to what extent you are aware of the facts of life. There are mysteries which are kept carefully hidden from children, and especially from girls. For girls should preserve their purity of mind, their spotless purity, until the moment when we surrender them to the arms of the man to whom their happiness is committed. It is for him to raise the veil. But if no whisper of these things has reached them, they recoil sometimes from the somewhat crude reality behind their dreams. Hurt and wounded, they refuse their husbands the absolute rights that are his by human and natural law. I cannot tell you more, my love. But do not forget this: you belong to your husband, entirely."<br /><br />This moment was preceded by 48 pages of chaste romance, walks in the country, meetings with the local priest, chit chat, rustic rural evocations. The beginning of the end of Jeanne's innocence is foreshadowed by this paragraph--which has been removed from some early editions!<br /><br />This is not a salacious novel, but it does address relations between many titled couples of independent means in nineteenth century Europe. It is not melodramatic, it moves briskly, it is full of historical detail and well-rounded characters.<br /><br />Tolstoy thought Maupassant an excellent writer and storyteller, but he was upset with him because he didn't moralize. Realism probably shouldn't moralize, or exaggerate. This is a must read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16436283808750787989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8196371261821528781">Lower 4 stars/upper 3 stars - I'm feeling generous. I did enjoy reading this. Jeanne was so naive and thought married life is like a storybook. It isn't, and her learning so was painful.<br/><br/><blockquote>She felt vexed with Julien for not understanding her feelings, and wondering at his want of delicacy; it raised a sort of barrier between them, and, for the first time, she understood that two people can never be in perfect sympathy; they may pass through life side by side, seemingly in perfect union, but neither</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8196371261821528781" style="display:none">Lower 4 stars/upper 3 stars - I'm feeling generous. I did enjoy reading this. Jeanne was so naive and thought married life is like a storybook. It isn't, and her learning so was painful.<br /><br /><blockquote>She felt vexed with Julien for not understanding her feelings, and wondering at his want of delicacy; it raised a sort of barrier between them, and, for the first time, she understood that two people can never be in perfect sympathy; they may pass through life side by side, seemingly in perfect union, but neither quite understands the other, and every soul must of necessity be for ever lonely.</blockquote><br /><br />This Guy de Maupassant's first of six novels. We know him more for his short stories. There are two other novels on the 1001 list, but I also want to find a collection of stories. This character study was quite good, and a short story is such a good medium for others. This novel also contained a good dose of his anti-Catholic sentiments, for those of you who might be offended by such.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9487784363672394903">Apart from one or two cliches, this was a closely observed, sad tale of a woman whose illusions of life are shattered by her cad of a husband. Interesting take on the role of religion in contemporary lives, with two different priests, one more 'live and let live', loved by the community, followed by an evangelical type who spies on illicit trysts and whose congregation dwindles. Maupassant, a brilliant short story writer, was a disciple of Flaubert, and this shows through in this tale of limited</span>
  <span id="freeText9487784363672394903" style="display:none">Apart from one or two cliches, this was a closely observed, sad tale of a woman whose illusions of life are shattered by her cad of a husband. Interesting take on the role of religion in contemporary lives, with two different priests, one more 'live and let live', loved by the community, followed by an evangelical type who spies on illicit trysts and whose congregation dwindles. Maupassant, a brilliant short story writer, was a disciple of Flaubert, and this shows through in this tale of limited lives in provincial France.</span>

<div id="review_125348261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125348261" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900147-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544395177p2/900147.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_214893273" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214893273" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5862550-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557438942p2/5862550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214893273?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/5862550-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140441611" href="/book/show/1032112.A_Woman_s_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5862550-sana?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214893273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11512266665953907584">The only other work I have read of Maupassant is his short story <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420275.The_Necklace' title='The Necklace by Guy de Maupassant' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Necklace</a> and I was instantly impressed by it. Thus, I bought A Woman's Life with high expectations and well, was left disappointed. What I would say about this novel is that A Woman's Life turned out to be a negative version of Jane Austen's portrayal of society in her novels. And not in a good way, really.<br/><br/>The world of Jeane is compacted to her home after her life in the convent. She is not much social and dreams of being in tr</span>
  <span id="freeText11512266665953907584" style="display:none">The only other work I have read of Maupassant is his short story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420275.The_Necklace" title="The Necklace by Guy de Maupassant" rel="nofollow noopener">The Necklace</a> and I was instantly impressed by it. Thus, I bought A Woman's Life with high expectations and well, was left disappointed. What I would say about this novel is that A Woman's Life turned out to be a negative version of Jane Austen's portrayal of society in her novels. And not in a good way, really.<br /><br />The world of Jeane is compacted to her home after her life in the convent. She is not much social and dreams of being in true love one day. She eventually marries and have some of the best and the worst experiences. But despite those experiences, she doesn't grow as a person or as a character so much that I wanted to shake her from her oblivion. I have never read a book with a more frustrating character as Jeane was in terms of her personality. Endurance, much? I don't think so.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After her marriage to Julien and all that came with it, she should have had the courage to leave him after finding out about the affair with her maid, Rosalie. The response of her father was downright shameful when it came to the observations of the priest about the whole situation. Yes, the reaction maybe fit for a 19th century extramarital affair and an illegitimate son but God, the whole thing was dealt with disgustingly. And to think that the Baron, as Jeane's father was the mellower of the characters. I was frustrated a great deal and even more so when there was <i>another</i> affair. <br /><br />Julien didn't have the audacity to stop having them and had the vulgarity of a man bent on having those affairs and treating Rosalie the way he did. He truly deserved the ending he received. Even Paul, for that matter. But that is yet another frustrating character to get into. As Jeane is just too naive to think otherwise of her detached husband and a manipulating son. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Yes, there were moments when she flashed fire and seemed strong enough to take on the world. But those were in a dwindling amount and so in the end, amounted to almost nothing. On some level, I can understand why she acted the way she did but I just think it was exaggerated. She craved affection a great deal; but at what price because there seems to be no limit placed on it. Or a limit that Jeane could be aware of.<br /><br />Suffice it to say that A Woman's Life didn't have the factor to make it beautiful to a reader. As apart from Jeane, the characters of the Baron and the Baroness, Julien and Paul turned out to be mere egg shells detached from the actual substance. Maybe short stories are better suited to Maupassant after all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11512266665953907584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125189878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125189878" />
    <a title="Sue Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3583076-sue-smith"><img alt="Sue Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272665985p2/3583076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125189878?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue Smith" href="/user/show/3583076-sue-smith">Sue Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140441611" href="/book/show/1032112.A_Woman_s_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3583076-sue-smith?shelf=books-read-in-2010">books-read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3583076-sue-smith?shelf=1001-books-before-you-die">1001-books-before-you-die</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125189878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3653174124079011201">I was genuinely surprised by this book. Not so much by the content of it, but by the fact that it was written with some insight by a man of the time who perhaps wouldn't have had that insight. <br/><br/>This book is not a happy book. Far from it. It's down right depressing. But it is an interesting peek into what a rural, priviledged woman's life would have been like in the late 1800's, where old ways and status are still influencing life. It also shows us how important it is to have far reaching dreams a</span>
  <span id="freeText3653174124079011201" style="display:none">I was genuinely surprised by this book. Not so much by the content of it, but by the fact that it was written with some insight by a man of the time who perhaps wouldn't have had that insight. <br /><br />This book is not a happy book. Far from it. It's down right depressing. But it is an interesting peek into what a rural, priviledged woman's life would have been like in the late 1800's, where old ways and status are still influencing life. It also shows us how important it is to have far reaching dreams and to never stop making them. To reach your dream is to stop life. You really need a purpose to keep yourself young at heart and healthy in mind. <br /><br />It also shows how important it is to not shelter your children from realities - they just get their hearts broken later - and that letting them go is the important thing to do (not easy - but important!). Coddling a child only creates a tyrant that no one can stand and then they grow up to be mean spirited adults.<br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book, despite the desparation of the character. It was disconcerting to see how frail her mind was with time and it made me think of my own life. With life, changes happen all the time and they aren't always to your liking. It's how you choose to handle them that makes all the difference in the world and in your mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3653174124079011201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3514520456" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3514520456" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5901350-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428956297p2/5901350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3514520456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10867969630972605697">A deeply depressing book about a young naive girl who ruined her life just by marrying without thinking about it long enough. How incredibly hard it was for a woman in nineteenth century to be happy! Even if she was noble and rich like Jeanne. I kept hoping for some kind of a hope for her and it came - but what the author undoubtedly thought of as a happy(ish)-end made me even more depressed.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14072986635238162385">This is a terrible book that reaffirms the old cliche that dudes can't write about women. It belongs it that long list. What a shame and a waste. <br/><br/>We don't have many true seducers among the great novelists. Probably because the Third Republic was the last time that you could tell a woman at a dinner party that you were a novelist, do it with a twinkle in your eye, and know you were going to get laid that same night.   <span id="freeText14072986635238162385" style="display:none">This is a terrible book that reaffirms the old cliche that dudes can't write about women. It belongs it that long list. What a shame and a waste. <br /><br />We don't have many true seducers among the great novelists. Probably because the Third Republic was the last time that you could tell a woman at a dinner party that you were a novelist, do it with a twinkle in your eye, and know you were going to get laid that same night. I want to believe that the seducer knows women well.<br /><br />Instead what we get is a kind of ideological letter to all the women Maupassant will still seduce in his short life: don't be naive, don't believe in love, and accept the bitterness of my seduction.<br /><br />My sense is that M. becomes not only a better novelist after this disaster, but makes a clear decision to write about something he knows about, himself, in his next and best novel Bel-Ami.</span>

<div id="review_2947371750" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2947371750" />
    <a title="George" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10168276-george"><img alt="George" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511867378p2/10168276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2947371750?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="George" class="user" itemprop="url" name="George" href="/user/show/10168276-george">George</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10168276-george?shelf=1001-books-list-read-2006">1001-books-list-read-2006</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2947371750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12323884172759079012">A well told, interesting, thought provoking short novel, (first published in 1883), about Jeanne, a daughter of a very well off French couple, (a Baron and Baroness). The writing style is very descriptive with many thought provoking sentences. The story starts slowly with detailed descriptions, introducing the main characters and Jeanne’s family property. <br/><br/>We firstly learn that Jeanne has been in a convent where she received five years of education. When she is 17 she leaves the convent to live o</span>
  <span id="freeText12323884172759079012" style="display:none">A well told, interesting, thought provoking short novel, (first published in 1883), about Jeanne, a daughter of a very well off French couple, (a Baron and Baroness). The writing style is very descriptive with many thought provoking sentences. The story starts slowly with detailed descriptions, introducing the main characters and Jeanne’s family property. <br /><br />We firstly learn that Jeanne has been in a convent where she received five years of education. When she is 17 she leaves the convent to live on her parent’s property on the coast of Normandy. The year is 1819. Shortly after she meets Julien Lamare. Within a short space of time she marries him. Jeanne quickly learns that life can be trying. The second half of the novel is filled with a number of dramatic events that impact Jeanne’s financially well off life style. A recommended read.<br /><br /><br />Here are some examples of the author’s writing style:<br /><br />‘Words dazzle and deceive because they are mimed by the face. But black words on a white page are the soul laid bare.’<br />‘Solitude is indeed dangerous for a working intelligence. We need to have around us people who think and speak. When we are alone for a long time we people the void with phantoms.’<br />‘It is the lives we encounter that make life worth living.’<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12323884172759079012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2788347881" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2788347881" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4599651-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472801929p2/4599651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2788347881?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/4599651-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140441611" href="/book/show/1032112.A_Woman_s_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4599651-ian?shelf=1001-books">1001-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2788347881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14777766455969006325">Poor Jeanne. De Maupassant creates a lovely fresh heroine: young, beautiful, with a convent education and a heart full of optimism and joy. Then he proceeds to lacerate her life with razor precision. Nothing and no one turns out as they should. The aristocratic layabout to whom she is married, her maid, even her mother's memory is tarnished. Priests are fickle and every act of generosity on Jeanne's part rebounds painfully. Her beloved son Paul turns out to be nothing but a trial to her. There i</span>
  <span id="freeText14777766455969006325" style="display:none">Poor Jeanne. De Maupassant creates a lovely fresh heroine: young, beautiful, with a convent education and a heart full of optimism and joy. Then he proceeds to lacerate her life with razor precision. Nothing and no one turns out as they should. The aristocratic layabout to whom she is married, her maid, even her mother's memory is tarnished. Priests are fickle and every act of generosity on Jeanne's part rebounds painfully. Her beloved son Paul turns out to be nothing but a trial to her. There is very little consolation for the reader. The book even manages to ruin Corsica as a honeymoon destination.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14777766455969006325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3107754854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3107754854" />
    <a title="Luke Feistamel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/94357649-luke-feistamel"><img alt="Luke Feistamel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598336790p2/94357649.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3107754854?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luke Feistamel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luke Feistamel" href="/user/show/94357649-luke-feistamel">Luke Feistamel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140441611" href="/book/show/1032112.A_Woman_s_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3107754854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14558287006339261668">Having read almost all of his 300 short stories, and this being only the 4th novel I've read from this author (clearly one of my favorite authors), proves he is much more prolific in short story writing. That doesn't mean he's not a great novelist as well. This protege of Flaubert, one of the greatest of all novelists who has not written many novels, can't have been expected to produce many novels in his life. That doesn't mean the novels Maupassant has written are not worth reading. Maupassant </span>
  <span id="freeText14558287006339261668" style="display:none">Having read almost all of his 300 short stories, and this being only the 4th novel I've read from this author (clearly one of my favorite authors), proves he is much more prolific in short story writing. That doesn't mean he's not a great novelist as well. This protege of Flaubert, one of the greatest of all novelists who has not written many novels, can't have been expected to produce many novels in his life. That doesn't mean the novels Maupassant has written are not worth reading. Maupassant has a style of writing richly detailed, plot-light stories, that engage you more than you could have imagined after reading the back cover snippet. There is much more in these novels than a copy-monkey can punch out in the exact short space editors allow to entice your mouth to water.<br />His novel-length prose can be described best as that he takes very complex characters, which were too complex for a short story, and spreads the characters over many more pages than the maximum allotted for short story space. So his novels are not every long, as they're more about exploring character beyond just a short format, but they are also not without their delight, especially to the reader with an interest to be taken away to a different world, particularly a coastal, Normandy world. But in the magic of the whole experience he doesn't forget those wonderful punchlines which wowed the reader of his short stories.<br />This, his first novel, though it lacks the more moralistic (or nihilistic) thrust of "Bel-Ami" or, my own favorite, and perhaps underrated, "Notre Coeur", (which I will review after I read it a second time), is definitely worth looking at.<br />If you don't enjoy the first two chapters, or expect the pace to speed up, I would say this novel is not for you, though you still might enjoy his many short stories which much more quickly get to the punch. What I love about Maupassant's longer works, however, is that they don't get to the punch, ever. There are punches in there, but they're only to your heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14558287006339261668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JRr+1TTvNGGUbtQpa+ChrLf4wDznC1/mFK9WAwR+fr3rYSO7EGJQmGI0SmRyyDWhgfAeSGWCc7YC7W9Tsw8MWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eaaiIj493bjXlqoIgWYG0LfFJi2Pp5au/xjAtC/POte33X9MGrC5QSHMNEWYTpLdgc34WQ0uuv7pWvnkmL5IMg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

C\'est un poème amoureux où les sentiments l\'emportent sur les convenances et la loi, un chant de désespoir et de révolte. À la création du Cid, le succès fut tel qu\'il fallut ajouter des chaises sur la scène. Depuis plus de trois siècles, il fait salle comble. Le théâtre de Corneille est fait de tendresse, d\'inattendu, de folie. On commence tout juste à le comprendre aujourd\'hui.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2508249354752478507\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18791.Guy_de_Maupassant">About Guy de Maupassant</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<span id="freeTextContainer16220616097443713537">Henri René Albert Guy de Maupassant was a popular 19th-century French writer. He is one of the fathers of the modern short story. A protege of Flaubert, Maupassant's short stories are characterized by their economy of style and their efficient effortless dénouement. He also wrote six short novels. A number of his stories often denote the futility of war and the innocent civilians who get crushed i</span>
  <span id="freeText16220616097443713537" style="display:none">Henri René Albert Guy de Maupassant was a popular 19th-century French writer. He is one of the fathers of the modern short story. A protege of Flaubert, Maupassant's short stories are characterized by their economy of style and their efficient effortless dénouement. He also wrote six short novels. A number of his stories often denote the futility of war and the innocent civilians who get crushed in it - many are set during the Franco-Prussian War of the 1870s.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16220616097443713537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
